s

reactions acting on the wheels are the same for both cases.

G

the back brakes are locked, and the front wheels are free to  0.6 m

| roll. Take m | =   | 0.3. |     |     |     |     |
| ------------ | --- | ---- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
s
A B
1 m 1.50 m
0.75 m

|           | A =        |                  | -               |                 | +    |     |

*8–8.

*8–12.
#
| If a torque of M |     | = 300 N m is applied to the flywheel, |     |     |     |     |
| ---------------- | --- | ------------------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
D
determine the force that must be developed in the hydraulic
| cylinder CD | to prevent the flywheel from rotating. |     |     | The |     |     |
| ----------- | -------------------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
coefficient of static friction between the friction pad at B
| and the flywheel is m |     | 0.4. |     |     |     |     |
| --------------------- | --- | ---- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
s =
0.6 m
1 m
30 B
C
60 mm A
0.3 m M   300 Nm
O
SOLUTION
Free-BodyDiagram:First we will consider the equilibrium of the flywheel using the
| free-body diagram shown in Fig.a.Here,the frictional force F |     |     |     | must act to the left to |     |     |
| ------------------------------------------------------------ | --- | --- | --- | ----------------------- | --- | --- |
B
produce the counterclockwise moment opposing the impending clockwise rotational
#
| motion caused by the 300 N                                     |                      | mcouple moment.Since the wheel is required to be on |               |                 |      |           |
| -------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------- | --------------------------------------------------- | ------------- | --------------- | ---- | --------- |
| the                                                            | verge  of  slipping, | then  F                                             | = m N = 0.4 N | . Subsequently, | the  | free-body |
|                                                                |                      | B                                                   | s B           | B               |      |           |
| diagram of member ABCshown in Fig.bwill be used to determine F |                      |                                                     |               |                 | .    |           |
CD
Equations of Equilibrium:We have
| a+©M | = 0; | 0.4 N (0.3) | - 300 = 0 | N = 2500 N |     |     |
| ---- | ---- | ----------- | --------- | ---------- | --- | --- |
|      | O    | B           |           | B          |     |     |
Using this result,
| a+©M | = 0; | F CD sin 30°(1.6) | + 0.4(2500)(0.06) | - 2500(1) | = 0 |     |

8–15. If the coefficient of static friction at contacting
surface between blocks A and B is m, and that betwee n
s
block B and bottom is 2m ,determine the inclination u at
s
which the identical blocks,each of weight W,begin to slide.
A
B
u
Solution
Free-Body Diagram. Here, we will assume that the impending motion of the upper block
is down the plane while the impending motion of the lower block is up the plane. Thus,
the frictional force F acting on the upper block acts up the plane while the friction forces
F and F ¿ acting on the lower block act down the plane as indicated on the free-body dia-
gram of the upper and lower blocks shown in Figs. a and b, respectively. Since both block
are required to be on the verge of slipping, then F = m s N and F′ = m s N′.
Equations of Equilibrium. Referring to Fig. a,
+cΣF y′ = 0; N - W cos u = 0 N = W cos u
+cΣF x′ = 0; T + m s W cos u - W sin u = 0 T = W sin u - m s W cos u
Using these results and1 referring2 to Fig. b,
+cΣF y ′ = 0; N′ - W cos u - W cos u = 0 N′ = 2W cos u
S + ΣF x ′ = 0; 2 W sin u - m s W cos u - m s W cos u - 2m s 2W cos u - W sin u = 0
1 sin u 2- 7m s cos u = 0 1 2
u = tan -17m s Ans.
Since the analysis yields a positive u, the above assumption is correct.
F(cid:6561)= 2μN(cid:6561)
s

*8–20.
The ring has a mass of 0.5 kg and is resting on the surface of  P
the table. In an effort to move the ring a normal force P from
the finger is exerted on it. If this force is directed towards the
B
ring’s center O as shown, determine its magnitude when the
ring is on the verge of slipping at A. The coefficient of static  60(cid:31)
O
| friction at A is m | = 0.2 and at B, m | = 0.3. |     |     |     |
| ------------------ | ----------------- | ------ | --- | --- | --- |
|                    | A                 | B      |     |     |     |
75 mm
A
Solution
|     | F A = F B     |             |             |     |     |
| --- | ------------- | ----------- | ----------- | --- | --- |
|     | P cos 60°     | F cos 30°   | F = 0       |     |     |

8–41.
Determine the minimum force P needed to push the tube E
E
up the incline. The force acts parallel to the plane, and the

A

P 30(cid:31)
B
C
Solution

S + ΣF x = 0; P - N A cos 30° - F A sin 30° - F C = 0 (1)
+cΣF y = 0; N C + F A cos 30° - N A sin 30° - 100(9.81) = 0 (2)
a+ΣM D = 0; F A (0.15) - F C (0.15) = 0 (3)
Also, for the FBD of the tube, Fig. b,
+QΣF x = 0; N A - F B - 40(9.81) sin 30° = 0 (4)
+a Σ F y = 0; N B - F A - 40(9.81) cos 30° = 0 (5)
a+ΣM E = 0; F A (0.15) - F B (0.15) = 0 (6)
Friction. Assuming that slipping is about to occur at A. Thus
F A = m A N A = 0.2 N A (7)
Solving Eqs. (1) to (7)
P = 285.97 N = 286 N Ans.
N A = 245.25 N N B = 388.88 N N C = 1061.15 N F A = F B = F C = 49.05 N
Since F B 6 (F B ) max = m B N B = 0.3(388.88) = 116.66 N and F C < (F C ) max = m C N C
= 0.4(1061.15) = 424.46 N, slipping indeed will not occur at B and C. Thus, the
assumption was correct.
Ans:

*8–56.
Determine the greatest angle (cid:88)so that the ladder does not
slip when it supports the 75-kg man in the position shown. C

friction at Aand Bis m s = 0.3.
u
G
2.5 m
2.5 m
A B
SOLUTION
Free-Body Diagram:The slipping could occur at either end Aor Bof the ladder.We
will assume that slipping occurs at end B.Thus,F B = m s N B = 0.3N B .
Equations of Equilibrium: Referring to the free-body diagram shown in Fig. b,
we have
:+ ©F x = 0; F BC sin u>2 - 0.3N B = 0
F BC sin u>2 = 0.3N B (1)
+c©F y = 0; N B - F BC cos u>2 = 0
F BC cos u>2 = N B (2)
Dividing Eq.(1) by Eq.(2) yields
tan u>2 = 0.3
u = 33.40° = 33.4° Ans.
Using this result and referring to the free-body diagram of member AC shown in
Fig.a,we have
a +©M A = 0; F BC sin 33.40°(2.5) - 75(9.81)(0.25) = 0 F BC = 133.66 N
33.40°
:+ ©F x = 0; F A - 133.66 sin ¢ 2 ≤ = 0 F A = 38.40 N
33.40°
+c©F y = 0; N A + 133.66 cos ¢ 2 ≤ - 75(9.81) = 0 N A = 607.73 N
Since F A 6 (F A ) max = m s N A = 0.3(607.73) = 182.32 N,end A will not slip.Thus,
the above assumption is correct.

u = 33.4°

8–62.
The wedge is used to level the member. Determine the 2 m
horizontal force P that must be applied to begin to push the 500 N/m
wedge forward. The coefficient of static friction between the
wedge and the two surfaces of contact is m s = 0.2. Neglect A
the weight of the wedge. P
B
5(cid:31)
1 m
C
Solution
Equations of Equilibrium and Friction. Since the wedge is required to be on the
verge to slide to the right, then slipping will have to occur at both of its contact
surfaces. Thus, F A = m s N A = 0.2 N A and F B = m s N B . Referring to the FBD
diagram of member AC shown in Fig. a
a+ΣM C = 0; 500(2)(1) - N A cos 5°(2) - N A sin 5°(1)
-0.2 N A cos 5°(1) + 0.2 N A sin 5°(2) = 0
N A = 445.65 N
Using this result and the FBD of the wedge, Fig. b,
+cΣF y = 0; N B - 445.65 cos 5° + 0.2(445.65) sin 5° = 0
N B = 436.18 N
S + ΣF x = 0; P - 0.2(445.65) cos 5° - 445.65 sin 5° - 0.2(436.18) = 0
P = 214.87 N = 215 N Ans.
Ans:
P =215 N
